EXAM QUESTION BANK

Create a paramedic question bank.

Include question types:

Multiple choice
Select all that apply
Clinical scenario
Medication calculation

Each question must include:

question
options
correct answer
rationale
category
difficulty

Example:

A paramedic arrives to a patient in respiratory distress with wheezing and accessory muscle use. Oxygen saturation is 86%.

What is the most appropriate first intervention?

Options
High flow oxygen
Nebulized salbutamol
Endotracheal intubation
IV epinephrine

Correct answer
High flow oxygen

Rationale
Initial management prioritizes oxygenation before advanced interventions.

GOAL

Build a production-ready PARAMEDIC BULK CONTENT INGESTION AND PUBLISHING SYSTEM for NurseNest so the admin can upload, validate, store, preview, edit, and publish large amounts of paramedic educational content safely and accurately.

This system must support bulk import of:
Lessons
Flashcards
Question bank items
Practice exams
Case scenarios
Glossary terms
SEO topic pages
Study guides
Category pages

This system must prevent content from being assigned to the wrong profession, wrong exam tier, wrong visibility level, or wrong site section.

PRIMARY OBJECTIVES

1. Allow fast bulk upload of paramedic content through admin
2. Validate content before publish
3. Prevent cross-tier contamination
4. Support drafts, preview, staged publish, and rollback
5. Support original SEO metadata per item
6. Make it easy for Erika to paste in large content sets without Replit misfiling them
7. Ensure uploaded content goes live on the published site, not just local/dev/admin preview
8. Support future scaling to more paramedic content without rebuilding the system

TOP-LEVEL CONTENT DOMAIN RULE

Create and enforce a top-level content domain field for every uploaded item:

contentDomain = "paramedic"

This field must be mandatory for all Paramedic Academy content.

Allowed contentDomain examples may include:
rn
rpn
np
rt
pharmacy-tech
paramedic

But for this build, you are implementing and enforcing:
paramedic

This field must be checked at:
database level if feasible
API validation layer
admin upload parser
frontend query filters
search filters
published page rendering
related content engine

If contentDomain is not "paramedic", it must not appear anywhere in the paramedic system.
If contentDomain is "paramedic", it must not appear in any non-paramedic learner-facing area unless explicit admin override exists.

FIELD MAPPING LAYER

Build a robust field mapping system.

This is critical.

When importing, the admin must be able to map incoming column names to expected schema fields.

Examples:
"Question" -> questionStem
"RationaleText" -> rationale
"Track" -> professionTrack
"SEO Title" -> seoTitle

The system must:
show detected columns
allow manual mapping
save reusable mapping templates
warn on unmapped required fields
allow transformation rules
show preview before final import

Create saved mapping templates for:
Lessons
Flashcards

VALIDATION ENGINE

Build a strong validation engine before import and before publish.

Validation must check:

GLOBAL
contentDomain must be paramedic
contentType must match selected import type
required fields present
slug uniqueness
title length reasonable
SEO title length reasonable
meta description present for SEO-visible content
visibility tier allowed
professionTrack allowed
region allowed
status allowed

must have title
must have intro

must have category

must have question
must have answer

must have rationale
for MCQ and SATA, must have options
must have a valid correctAnswer

must have debrief

must have definition

status = published

has at least minimum metadata
passes visibility rules

PREVENTING CROSS-TIER CONTAMINATION

This is one of the most important requirements.

Implement hard filters so that:
Paramedic content only appears in paramedic routes
RN content never appears in paramedic routes
RPN content never appears in paramedic routes
NP content never appears in paramedic routes
RT content never appears in paramedic routes
Pharmacy tech content never appears in paramedic routes

This must be enforced in:
backend queries

homepage and hub page cards
exam builders
flashcard deck builders
lesson filters
practice exam assembly
SEO page related content rails

Do not rely only on UI filtering.
Enforce in backend/database query logic too.

PUBLISHING TO LIVE SITE

The system must publish to the actual live published site data source, not just to a local builder state, not just to admin preview, and not just to dev-mode cache.

Audit the current content publishing workflow.
Fix the issue where content exists in admin/Replit but is not visible on the live site.

Ensure there is a single reliable publish pipeline:
draft content stored in DB
published content stored in DB
frontend reads from correct published DB/API source
cache invalidation occurs if needed
newly published content appears on live routes
sitemap updates if relevant
search indexes update if relevant

Add a publish confirmation log that confirms:
item imported
item validated
item stored
item published
frontend route available
sitemap updated if applicable

You are an expert exam-platform engineer, educational product designer, psychometric UX strategist, and React developer working inside the existing NurseNest codebase.

STACK
Frontend: React + Vite + Wouter
Backend: Node + Express
Database: PostgreSQL

ABSOLUTE RULES
Do not restructure the existing platform.
Do not break RN, RPN, NP, RT, pharmacy tech, or existing Paramedic content systems.
Do not remove role gating or paywalls.
Do not copy any official exam branding, logos, copyrighted text, exact proprietary layouts, or trademarked visuals.
Do not claim this is the official NREMT, COPR, PCP, or ACP exam.
Do not use protected organization names in a misleading way in learner-facing UI.
This must be a simulator inspired by the real test experience, not a counterfeit copy.

GOAL

Build a HIGH-FIDELITY PARAMEDIC EXAM SIMULATOR inside NurseNest that feels extremely close to the real test-taking experience for paramedic learners while remaining legally safe and original.

This should support:
General Paramedic
PCP-style prep
ACP-style prep
NREMT-style prep

The simulator should feel like a professional computer-based exam:
clean
minimal
high pressure but organized
one question at a time
clear timer
flag for review
question navigator
review screen
submit screen
rationale hidden in exam mode
progress visible but not distracting

DESIGN TARGET

The exam UI should feel like a real professional testing center interface:
plain white or very light background
minimal pastel NurseNest accents only in small areas
clean sans-serif typography
no clutter
no marketing banners during exam mode
no oversized decorative cards during active testing
no soft consumer-app dashboard aesthetic inside the actual exam player

IMPORTANT
Outside the exam player, keep NurseNest aesthetic.
Inside the exam player, switch to an exam-safe minimalist mode:
clinical white
very light gray borders
small muted lavender/teal highlights only for active states
simple rectangular panels
subtle shadows or none
high readability
clear spacing
no playful design

EXAM EXPERIENCE TO EMULATE

Build the simulator so it matches the BEHAVIOR of modern paramedic computer exams as closely as possible:

1. Candidate lands on pre-exam instructions screen
2. Candidate sees tutorial/help on question types
3. Candidate starts exam
4. One question displays at a time
5. Candidate can go Next and Previous if mode allows
6. Candidate can flag item for review
7. Candidate sees question number and remaining count
8. Candidate sees timer if enabled
9. Candidate can open an item list / navigator
10. Candidate can review flagged/unanswered items before final submit
11. Candidate gets confirmation before final submission
12. Candidate sees score report or practice feedback depending on mode

EXAM MODES

Create separate modes:

1. PRACTICE MODE
Shows rationale after submission or at end depending on settings
Allows tutor hints if enabled
Can reveal weak areas
Can allow pause/resume

2. EXAM MODE
No rationale during testing
No hints
Minimal navigation based on selected rules
Strict timer
Full-screen focused feel
Review screen before final submission
Results only after submit

3. ADAPTIVE SIMULATION MODE
Simulates changing difficulty based on performance
Does NOT claim to be official CAT unless true
Label it:
Adaptive Exam-Style Simulation
Use weighted difficulty progression and domain balancing

IMPORTANT
Do not falsely claim official CAT scoring logic or exact official algorithm.
Create an exam-style adaptive engine that feels realistic and rigorous.

QUESTION TYPES TO SUPPORT

Support:
single best answer multiple choice
multiple response / select all that apply
scenario-linked item sets
drag and drop sequencing
build list / ordered response
hotspot-style image questions if supported
bowtie-style logic only if already supported by platform
medication calculation
ECG interpretation
waveform interpretation
vital-sign trend interpretation

QUESTION TYPE UI RULES

Each item type must have its own clean renderer.

Single Best Answer:
radio buttons
one selected only

Multiple Response:
checkboxes
clear instruction that more than one may be correct

Ordered Response:
drag list or move up/down controls
clear locked order validation

Scenario Sets:
persistent left or top scenario stem
multiple linked questions underneath
ability to move between linked items without losing context

Image/Hotspot:
zoomable but lightweight
clear click target
mobile fallback if exact hotspot is difficult

Waveform/ECG:
high-resolution SVG-based rendering
not blurry screenshots
scalable on desktop
optional zoom
brand-neutral medical monitor styling
not cartoonish

REALISM REQUIREMENTS

The simulator should feel realistic in these ways:
question density similar to a real exam screen
limited distractions
consistent button placement
persistent timer in top bar
persistent flag control
question counter
answer choices spaced like a real testing platform
clear review status indicators:
answered
unanswered
flagged
current

Do not make it look like a quiz app.
Do not use bright colors or giant rounded cards in exam mode.
Do not show celebratory confetti or gamified animations during exam mode.

SCREEN FLOW

Build these screens:

1. Exam Launch Screen
Exam title
track
number of questions
time limit
mode
instructions
start button

2. Item Type Tutorial Screen
Show sample of:
single answer

3. Active Exam Screen

exam title

question numbers

4. Review Screen
Counts:
answered
unanswered
flagged
remaining
buttons:
return to items
submit exam

5. Submit Confirmation Modal
clear warning:
you cannot change answers after submitting

6. Results Screen
For practice mode:
score
domain performance
rationales
weak areas
review missed items

For exam mode:
minimal result summary or configurable delayed review

QUESTION NAVIGATION RULES

Support configurable navigation profiles:
Free Navigation
Forward Only
Section-Based Navigation

Default for NurseNest:
Practice Mode = Free Navigation
Exam Mode = Free Navigation or configurable by exam template

QUESTION STATUS INDICATORS

Use these statuses:
not visited

flagged
answered + flagged

Display these clearly in the navigator.

TIMER SYSTEM

Build a reliable exam timer:
countdown from total time
warning state near end
auto-submit if time expires if enabled
pause disabled in exam mode
pause optional in practice mode

Persist timer state safely in local storage/session plus backend if needed for resume in practice mode.

ANTI-CLUTTER UX RULES

During active exam:
hide site nav
hide marketing footer
hide unrelated sidebars
hide popups
hide upsell banners
hide decorative illustrations

Allow only:
top exam bar
question area
navigator
exam controls

mixed full-length finals

BLUEPRINT-STYLE WEIGHTING

Do not claim exact official weighting unless sourced and confirmed.
Instead use configurable blueprint-based weighting with admin controls.

Create default balanced weighting across:
Airway / Respiration / Ventilation
Cardiology / Resuscitation
Trauma
Medical / OB / Pediatrics
Operations / Safety
Pharmacology where applicable

Allow admin to edit weighting per exam template.

ADAPTIVE SIMULATION ENGINE

Create an adaptive exam-style mode:
start with moderate difficulty
if candidate answers correctly, modestly increase likelihood of harder next item
if incorrect, shift toward moderate or lower difficulty
maintain domain balance
prevent overexposure of same subcategory
do not reveal adaptation to learner during test

Label clearly in UI:
Adaptive Exam-Style Simulation
Do not say official CAT unless it is actually official.

QUESTION BANK SEPARATION

US-only if tied to NREMT-style framing or U.S. terminology

Never mix these silently.
Always filter by region and track in:
exam assembly

You are working inside the NurseNest codebase.

Your task is to generate structured content generation tools and import-ready datasets for the Medical Laboratory Technology (MLT / MLS) platform for both Canada and the United States.

This system must support:
- question banks
- flashcards
- lessons
- study plans
- blog content
- free sample pages
- subscription landing pages
- remediation linking
- adaptive exam practice
- realistic exam simulators

All content must be structured for direct import into the NurseNest admin dashboard.

Do not generate mockups. Generate structured JSON-ready content generation systems.

The platform must support both tracks:

Canada:
CSMLS-style MLT exam prep

United States:
ASCP-style MLT / MLS exam prep

-------------------------------------

Create structured discipline tags for:

professional_practice

CORE MODES

Build 4 exam modes:

1. Practice Mode
- can be timed or untimed
- can show rationale after each question or only at end depending on settings
- can allow hints if enabled
- can allow pause/resume
- can show domain breakdown after submission
- can show weak-area recommendations

2. Exam Mode
- timed by default
- no rationale during exam
- no hints
- focused minimalist interface
- review screen before final submit
- clear final submission warning
- result summary after completion

3. Adaptive Exam-Style Mode
- difficulty changes based on performance
- maintain domain coverage
- no claim of official CAT scoring
- label clearly as:
Adaptive Exam-Style Simulation
- should feel rigorous and realistic
- do not expose algorithm details to learner during exam

4. Drill Mode
- shorter focused sets by domain
- e.g. Airway Drill, Trauma Drill, Cardiology Drill
- fast-launch experience
- useful for quick review

QUESTION WRITING RULES

Every waveform question must:
- reference the waveform meaningfully
- require interpretation, not just decoration
- be clinically plausible
- have realistic distractors
- avoid nonsense answer choices
- have a rationale that teaches the learner why the answer is correct
- connect to prehospital care where appropriate
- avoid claiming official exam wording
- sound like NurseNest educational content, not a textbook excerpt

DO NOT write vague questions like:
“What does this show?”
without enough context.

DO write stronger versions like:
“Which interpretation of this rhythm strip is most concerning for immediate instability?”
or
“Which capnography pattern is most consistent with bronchospasm in this patient?”

QUESTION USE CASES

1. Pure Recognition

2. Clinical Priority
Example:

3. Trend Interpretation
Example:
What does the change in this monitor trend most suggest?

4. Post-Intervention Interpretation
Example:
Which change after intervention suggests improvement?

5. Scenario-Linked Reasoning
Example:
Given this patient presentation and waveform, what is the best interpretation?

6. Multi-Signal Interpretation
Example:
This patient has hypotension, tachycardia, and this waveform trend. What is most concerning?

specific
educational
not generic
not repetitive

2. explain why that matters clinically
3. explain why distractors are less appropriate if useful

Bad rationale example:
“This is correct because it is correct.”

Do not do that.

QUESTION WRITING RULES

All questions must:
- be original
- be clinically plausible
- sound like real prehospital reasoning questions
- focus on recognition, prioritization, interpretation, reassessment, and intervention logic
- avoid unrealistic hospital-only detail unless clearly relevant
- avoid meaningless trivia
- avoid silly distractors
- avoid vague stems
- avoid overclaiming exact official exam style
- be useful in both learning and simulation contexts

Distractors must be plausible.
Do not write ridiculous wrong answers.

GOOD DISTRACTOR EXAMPLE
For chest pain:
musculoskeletal chest wall pain
panic-related symptoms
benign mild discomfort
possible ACS

BAD DISTRACTOR EXAMPLE
banana poisoning
sprained elbow
sunburn
paper cut

Do not do that.

QUESTION STYLE GUIDELINES

Questions should often test:
- first priority
- red flag recognition
- deterioration recognition
- difference between stable and unstable
- ABC prioritization
- interpretation of symptom clusters
- pattern recognition
- reassessment logic
- common prehospital pitfalls
- safe clinical thinking

Use common stem styles like:
- Which finding is most concerning?
- What is the best interpretation?
- What should the paramedic suspect?
- Which action is most appropriate first?
- Which findings support this concern? Select all that apply.
- What change most strongly suggests deterioration?
- Which patient is most unstable?
- Which finding is least consistent with this condition?

RATIONALE RULES

Every rationale must be:
2 to 5 sentences
specific
educational
not repetitive boilerplate

Good rationale structure:
1. identify the core clinical interpretation
2. explain why that answer fits best
3. briefly explain why other options are less appropriate when useful

Do not use:
"This is correct because it is correct."
Do not use:
"This answer is right."

Freeform educational explanation is required.

SCENARIO QUESTION RULES

For clinical-scenario items:
- write a short but meaningful case
- include age/sex only when helpful
- include relevant vitals or symptoms when helpful
- keep it prehospital-focused
- end with a specific decision or interpretation question

For scenario stems, do not write huge walls of text.
Aim for concise but realistic.

EXAMPLES OF GOOD SCENARIO FORMAT
"A 68-year-old patient with chest pressure becomes pale, diaphoretic, and hypotensive during transport. What is the best interpretation?"
"A child with respiratory distress is becoming quieter and more fatigued. What is the most concerning explanation?"

Diabetic Emergencies
- Which symptoms suggest hypoglycemia?
- Why should glucose be checked in altered mental status?

Stroke
- Why is rapid stroke recognition important?

REGIONAL NOTE SYSTEM

Example:
regionNotes = {
  "Canada": [
    {
      "label": "Canada Note",
      "content": "Canadian PCP and ACP learners should ..."
    }
  ],
  "US": [
    {
      "label": "U.S. Note",
      "content": "U.S. EMT and paramedic learners should ..."
    }
  ]
}

RULES
- General lesson content should remain shared where possible

You are an expert EMS clinical educator, psychometric exam item writer, large-scale question bank architect, and full stack database-aware content generator working inside the NurseNest codebase.

STACK
Frontend: React + Vite + Wouter
Backend: Node + Express
Database: PostgreSQL

ABSOLUTE RULES

Do not restructure the platform.
Do not overwrite existing question banks.
Do not break the paramedic exam simulator.
Do not produce placeholder text.
Do not generate vague questions.
Do not produce weak rationales.
Do not generate impossible clinical scenarios.
Do not mix Canadian and U.S. terminology incorrectly.

Everything must be original, clinically plausible, and production-ready.

---

GOAL

Generate a MASSIVE PARAMEDIC QUESTION BANK for NurseNest.

Total questions target:

Minimum: 1,500  
Preferred: 2,000–3,000  

This question bank must support:

Practice questions
Topic drills
Mock exams
Adaptive exam simulation
Remediation learning

---

QUESTION TYPES

Use a mix of:

Single best answer (multiple-choice)
Select-all-that-apply
Clinical scenario questions
Ordered-response questions

Distribution example:

60% multiple-choice  
20% select-all-that-apply  
15% clinical scenario  
5% ordered response

---

DIFFICULTY DISTRIBUTION

Introductory: 30%  
Intermediate: 50%  
Advanced: 20%

Advanced questions should include more clinical reasoning and scenario interpretation.

---

QUESTION DOMAINS

Distribute questions across these domains:

Airway / Ventilation
Respiratory Emergencies
Cardiology / Resuscitation
Shock / Perfusion
Trauma
Neurology / Stroke
Pediatrics
Obstetrics
Medical Emergencies
Pharmacology
Toxicology
Diabetic Emergencies
Operations / Scene Safety
Patient Assessment
Vital Signs Interpretation

Target roughly 100–200 questions per domain.

---

CONTENT MODEL

Each question must include these fields:

contentDomain
questionStem
questionType
questionInstruction
options
correctAnswer
rationale
category
subcategory
tags
relatedTopicSlug
professionTrack
region
visibilityTier
difficulty
examRelevance
status
simulationEligible
scenarioSetId
waveformAssetId

---

FIELD RULES

contentDomain must always be "paramedic"

region allowed values:
General
Canada
US

professionTrack allowed values:
General-Paramedic
PCP
ACP
EMT
Paramedic

status:
draft

simulationEligible:
true

waveformAssetId:
null for non-waveform questions

scenarioSetId:
null unless the question is part of a scenario group

---

REGION DISTRIBUTION

General questions: ~70%

Canada-specific questions: ~15%

U.S.-specific questions: ~15%

---

CANADA QUESTIONS

Use:

PCP terminology
ACP terminology
Canadian exam preparation context
mmol/L glucose values

Avoid:

U.S. terminology
mg/dL glucose values

---

US QUESTIONS

Use:

EMT terminology
Paramedic terminology
U.S. exam-style wording
mg/dL glucose values

Avoid:

Canadian terminology
mmol/L glucose values

---

SCENARIO QUESTIONS

Clinical scenario questions must include:

patient presentation
relevant symptoms
relevant vital signs when appropriate
prehospital context
clear clinical reasoning question

Do not make scenarios excessively long.

Example:

"A 67-year-old patient with chest pressure becomes pale and diaphoretic during transport. Blood pressure drops to 90/60 mmHg. What is the most concerning interpretation?"

---

QUESTION STYLE RULES

Questions should test:

recognition of critical findings
prioritization of care
pattern recognition
interpretation of symptoms
deterioration recognition
assessment logic
clinical reasoning
prehospital decision-making

Avoid trivial memorization questions.

---

DISTRACTOR RULES

Distractors must be plausible.

Incorrect answers should represent:

common mistakes
less likely interpretations
misleading symptoms

Do not create obviously ridiculous distractors.

---

RATIONALE RULES

Each rationale must:

be 2–4 sentences
explain why the answer is correct
briefly explain why other options are less appropriate
teach the concept

Bad example:

"This answer is correct."

Good example:

"This presentation suggests worsening perfusion due to hypotension and diaphoresis. These findings often indicate cardiovascular compromise rather than simple musculoskeletal discomfort."

---

FREE VS PREMIUM DISTRIBUTION

Free questions: 200  
Premium questions: remaining questions

Free questions should represent multiple domains.

Do not make free questions extremely easy only.

---

TAGGING RULES

Use meaningful tags such as:

airway
ventilation
shock
perfusion
trauma
stroke
diabetic
respiratory
cardiology
scene-safety
assessment
vital-signs
pharmacology
pediatrics

---

LESSON LINKING

Each question must include a relatedTopicSlug.

Example values:

airway-management-fundamentals
shock-assessment-in-prehospital-care
chest-pain-assessment-for-paramedics
stroke-recognition-in-the-field
anaphylaxis-management-overview
diabetic-emergencies-overview
trauma-primary-survey
scene-safety-for-paramedics
vital-signs-interpretation

---

OUTPUT FORMAT

Return questions in structured JSON format:

{
 "generalQuestions": [...],
 "canadaQuestions": [...],
 "usQuestions": [...]
}

Each array should contain question objects following the schema.

---

BATCH GENERATION

Generate questions in batches of 100–200 per output to avoid truncation.

Ensure questions do not repeat across batches.

---

QUALITY VALIDATION

Before returning any batch:

Check for:

duplicate questions
missing fields
incorrect units
weak rationales
unrealistic scenarios

Fix all issues before output.

---

FINAL RULE

Do not include explanation outside the JSON except a final count line:

General: X | Canada: Y | US: Z | Total: N



Audit the generated question batch and reject any question that fails these checks:

1. Missing schema fields
2. Incorrect region unit system
3. Weak or generic rationale
4. Unrealistic clinical scenario
5. Duplicate question concept
6. Distractors that are obviously incorrect
7. Question not clearly related to paramedic practice
8. Missing relatedTopicSlug
9. simulationEligible not set to true
10. Overly long scenario text

Repair all failed questions before returning the final JSON batch.
